Some people aren't quite getting why some people are mad. It's not that Cody lost, it's that Roman won. The fact is that at this time him having the title isn't helping or building up anyone. Also its the same thing everytime. Roman comes in, looks dominant for the first half of the match, starts to see that his opponent is greater than he thought, and he may have underestimated them, and then someone comes in and takes out Roman's opponent for him. It has happened in every defense at this point. That is not good story telling. And that is the issue with the Uso's having their titles as well. KO and Sami NEEDED to win Saturday night, at the very least for the health of the titles. The days where 800, 900, 1,000 day reigns (pun intended) are long gone, as they were a product of the territory era. At this point, the best thing they can do is this: Roman starts to gloat about how he won, and how he still values his cousins, even though they couldn't get the job done. Adam Pierce arrives and says "Roman, this is ridicules at this point. They may have lost, but at least they did it on their own. Your next defense will have a special stipulation. There will be multiple refs, and while your opponent will still need to beat you via pin or submission, if you win by count out or DQ, you will be stripped of the titles." The next match comes, it starts to go through the same formula. Dominant Roman, starts to realize he underestimated his foe, etc. Paul Hayman and Solo try to distract the refs, but one isn't having any of it. The Uso's run out, thinking they are clear and super kicking Roman's opponent. Bell rings, the other ref saw it all.  Roman is LIVID. He blames Jimmy and Jey. He tells them they need to win back their titles. They don't. Roman starts to become paranoid. Its Sammy all over again. They are trying to sabotage him. He orders Solo to take care of it. Solo refuses. They are his brothers. Roman snaps. Jimmy, Jey, and Solo abandon him. Paul Haymen continues to whisper in Roman's ear. They betrayed him. They need to be taught not to go against their tribal chief. He starts taking them out one by one. Its not attacks, not to him, its punishment. They sabotaged him, they failed him. He is the tribal chief. He is unraveling. Rakishi tries to talk to him. "Roman, this isn't you. Roman you need to stop" Roman agrees. He needs to stop. He needs to stop letting the tribe betray him. He takes out Rikishi. Roman appears in front of the crowd. He is the tribal chief, and they will acknowledge him, after all the family already has in the past. He has forced everyone in the family to acknowledge him. He is the tribal chief. There is no one in the family that is better, that has more power than him. Then it happens, it finally happens. "IF YA SMELL!!!" Rock comes out. He has been watching. He has been busy and has not been able to deal with the situation. Three years he let it get out of hand, but enough is enough. Rock looks Roman in the eye and says the one thing Roman has not heard anyone say yet. "I do not acknowledge you." Roman smirks his cocky smirk, and him and the Rock laugh, and then Roman goes for a shot at the Rock, only to get a Rock bottom. Its set, Roman vs. Rock. And Roman... looses. This gets the title on someone else and allows for the buildup of someone else, finally gives us the Roman v. Rock match they have been dangling for YEARS. And it gives Roman a fresh start, from here he can go on to be an unhinged heel, in total denial of what happened, or it lets him start to see the error of his ways and start to become a face again. But also what it does is that if Roman DOES want time away, it gives him an out to do so.

Those of you who wanted Cody to win, may I ask for your reasoning other than it was supposed to be his "moment"? This is a guy who came back to this company a year ago, had a few matches with Seth Rollins, which he all won, proceeded to sit out the rest of the year due to his torn pec, comes back at the Rumble in January at the number 30 spot, wins effortlessly, and was supposed to just take the titles from not just the WWE's top guy but a a champion in the middle of one of the most intriguing and well-presented storylines in WWE history. I don't see the logic. I don't have a problem with Cody dethroning Roman, but WrestleMania wasn't it. He can slay the king at SummerSlam or whatever. The Usos losing is a crack in the Bloodline's armour. This will allow their friction from late 2020 to resurface which will inevitably make the distance between them grow more and more and simultaneously you keep Cody involved and eventually he can have his "moment".   For most of you people, it's all about the instant gratification. Clash at the Castle, Drew should've won because it was in his home turf and he didn't get his proper WrestleMania moment.. Sami Zayn should've won at Elimination Chamber because he's super over and the match was in his hometown. There's no rationality here. It's pure emotion.  This is a final boss that reminds me of Thanos and Kingpin. If the formation of the Bloodline was a slow build, then the dissolution of the Bloodline also needs a slow build. Now one may argue Roman losing both titles tonight would've contributed to this slow downfall of the Bloodline and I agree. Seeing Roman lose and become absolutely unhinged by not only taking out Cody but also taking out the Usos and Sikoa would've been absolutely phenomenal television, but like I mentioned earlier, the manner in which Cody has been inserted into this whole storyline, it would be a disservice to just hand it all to him on a silver platter for the sake of giving him his "moment" and him "finishing the story". The story will finish. Just not at 'Mania.
